<div id="review_923840339" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/923840339" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/923840339?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17878613-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Gillian Flynn </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer923840339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8229030553089458650">I can consider this one of the few messed up novels that amazed me by its darkness. Some of the other ones were Gone Girl and Dark Places, so I guess I do have to agree with the blurb from Wall street journal stating that this is a European Gone Girl. <br/><br/>This is one of those circumstances wherein I'm glad I didn't listen to the bad reviews, and the low overall rating of the novel. Opinions vary, so stick with your gut. If the novel seems like something you'd enjoy, then don't hesitate to give it a </span>
  <span id="freeText8229030553089458650" style="display:none">I can consider this one of the few messed up novels that amazed me by its darkness. Some of the other ones were Gone Girl and Dark Places, so I guess I do have to agree with the blurb from Wall street journal stating that this is a European Gone Girl. <br /><br />This is one of those circumstances wherein I'm glad I didn't listen to the bad reviews, and the low overall rating of the novel. Opinions vary, so stick with your gut. If the novel seems like something you'd enjoy, then don't hesitate to give it a read.<br /><br />Halfway through the novel I decided to consider this as the epitome of contemporary fiction, among all the novels that I've read so far. It's weird how endless ramblings regarding random things in life kept my attention for more than 100+ pages. Palahniuk tried that style with me, but failed miserably. Koch on the other hand managed to make me like the novel even more because of the rambling. I cared about what he was trying to point out, and everything the main character said only made me like him better.<br /><br />This novel, like I said, was messed up. If you're not a fan of dark fiction, then I'd suggest you avoid this. It's not gut-wrenching in the same way as some gore-y horror movies, but the outcome would make you question the sanity of the characters, or even the author himself. I'm a fan of out of norm fiction, so that means I don't mind if the author tackles on topics that are profane and socially unacceptable. I'm not one to promote such activities, of course, because I'm against them, but writing about those doesn't mean that the author automatically thinks that it's supposed to be right. <br /><br />The plot took a while for it to develop. Halfway through I honestly still didn't know what was the main focus of the novel. The secret wasn't revealed then and I was impatiently waiting for it to be discussed further. At first I thought that the novel was going to have a terrible plot because of its seemingly nonexistent development, but thankfully I was proven wrong.<br /><br />The characters were the main reason why this novel was messed up. Let me add in the fact though that messed up doesn't mean it was bad. I mean messed up in a positive way. Psychologically challenged characters are the best to read about, at least for me. Paul, Claire, Serge, and Babette were all amazing, and fully developed in the end. One or two of the four truly shocked me in the end of the novel. I didn't expect them to develop the way they did but the author knew what he was doing.<br /><br />In the end one may ask, "What was this truly about?". In my opinion, it was about how one would do anything to keep their family safe, no matter what the consequences may be. The love of a couple for their child, and how nothing can stand against that.<br /><br />4.5/5 stars. Why round it down? It's because I needed more. The novel felt like it was cut short too early. The ending was not ambiguous, and I liked what happened in the end. It does feel like a European Gone Girl, so get ready for messed up to the tenth power. Highly recommended for psychological thriller fans, because this felt like a mixture of contemporary and psycho-thriller. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8229030553089458650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3026592778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15068376846871513852">The Dinner, Herman Koch<br/>The story is narrated by Paul Lohman, a former history teacher. He and his wife Claire meet at a fancy restaurant in Amsterdam with his elder brother Serge, a prominent politician and contender for the position of Dutch prime minister, and his wife Babette. The plan is to discuss over dinner how to handle a crime committed by their teenage sons, Michel and Rick, respectively. The violent act of the two boys had been filmed by a security camera and shown on TV, but, so far,</span>
  <span id="freeText15068376846871513852" style="display:none">The Dinner, Herman Koch<br />The story is narrated by Paul Lohman, a former history teacher. He and his wife Claire meet at a fancy restaurant in Amsterdam with his elder brother Serge, a prominent politician and contender for the position of Dutch prime minister, and his wife Babette. The plan is to discuss over dinner how to handle a crime committed by their teenage sons, Michel and Rick, respectively. The violent act of the two boys had been filmed by a security camera and shown on TV, but, so far, they have not been identified. The parents have to decide on what to do. They debate over dinner causing tension throughout the evening. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و هفتم ماه اکتبر سال 2018 میلادی<br />عنوان: شام مخصوص؛ نویسنده: هرمان کخ؛ مترجم: مهرنوش گلشاهی‌فر؛ ویرایش: مریم سعیدی؛ تهران : ستاک‏‫، 1396؛ در 284 ص؛ شابک: 9786009641864؛ چاپ دیگر: 1397؛ در 295 ص؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان هلندی - سده 21 م<br /><br />فهرست: نوشیدنی قبل از غذا؛ غذای اصلی؛ نوشیدنی بعد از غذا؛ انعام<br /><br />داستان از آن جایی آغاز میشود، که در یک عصر تابستان دو برادر، به همراه همسران خویش، بر سر میز شامی بنشسته‌ اند، و در تلاشند یکی از مهم‌ترین تصمیمات زندگی خود را بگیرند، این چهار تن درباره‌ ی واقعیتی، که ذهن آن‌ها را به خود درگیر کرده، گفتگو می‌کنند. نقل نمونه متن: «یکشنبه بعد از ظهر، پنج روز بعد از شروع اثر داروها، روی مبل سالن خانه دراز کشیده بودم، و روزنامه می‌خواندم. از در شیشه‌ ای که به حیاط باز می‌شد، می‌توانستم ببینم که باران شروع به باریدن کرده‌ است. آسمان آن روز آبی با ابرهای سفید لکه‌ ای بود. باید بگویم که این اواخر از اینکه در خانه‌ ی خودم، در سالن، روی مبل نشسته باشم ترس برم می‌داشت. ترسم ناشی از حسی بود، که نسبت به افراد دیگر در شرایط مشابه به خودم داشتم. اینکه صدها نفر دیگر مثل من در خانه‌ شان روی مبل دراز کشیده‌ اند. بیشتر وقت‌ها در تاریکی به این فکر می‌کردم، که حالا که همه‌ ی آدم‌ها در خانه‌ شان هستند، چه اتفاقی می‌افتد. از جایی که روی مبل دراز کشیده بودم، نمی‌توانستم کسی ‌را ببینم، چون بوته‌ های سبزی جلوی پنجره بودند؛ ولی همین حسی که پشت این بوته‌ ها، خانه‌ های دیگری بودند، و پشت پنجره‌ های دیگر هم آدم‌هایی مثل من دراز کشیده‌ اند، و یا نشسته‌ اند، حس خفقان خاصی را به من منتقل می‌کرد. باید بگویم از مردم و یا بهتر بگویم آدم‌ها ترس نداشتم. از داشتن شرایط مشابه هراس داشتم. از تکرار وضعیت همانندمان می‌ترسیدم. به هر صورت قبل از استفاده از این داروها آدمی نبودم که بخواهم در جشن‌ها، و یا دورهمی‌های دوستانه، خودنمایی بکنم، و یا مجلس را با خوش صحبتیم بچرخانم. بیشتر شبیه کسی بودم که دلش می‌خواهد گوشه‌ گیری بکند، جایی بنشیند و با کسی حرف نزند. باید بگویم اینجوری متفاوت بودم.»؛ پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="15068376846871513852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609831634" />
    <a title="RandomAnthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/721021-randomanthony"><img alt="RandomAnthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470919631p2/721021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/609831634?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RandomAnthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RandomAnthony" href="/user/show/721021-randomanthony">RandomAnthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer609831634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2052585462198221569">I understand comparing a book to <i>Gone Girl</i> will push sales, so yay for that comparison plastered on every <i>The Dinner</i> reference. But seriously, motherfuckers, this novel is more like Flynn's <i>Sharp Objects</i> and, in my eyes, better than <i>Gone Girl</i>. So let's stop talking about <i>Gone Girl</i>, even though I liked that book, because, you know, there are other books in the goddamn universe and I'm trying to review one as we speak.<br/><br/><i>The Dinner</i>'s main character is an angry, reflective guy out at a restaurant with</span>
  <span id="freeText2052585462198221569" style="display:none">I understand comparing a book to <i>Gone Girl</i> will push sales, so yay for that comparison plastered on every <i>The Dinner</i> reference. But seriously, motherfuckers, this novel is more like Flynn's <i>Sharp Objects</i> and, in my eyes, better than <i>Gone Girl</i>. So let's stop talking about <i>Gone Girl</i>, even though I liked that book, because, you know, there are other books in the goddamn universe and I'm trying to review one as we speak.<br /><br /><i>The Dinner</i>'s main character is an angry, reflective guy out at a restaurant with his wife, brother, and sister-in-law. The action unfolds over the evening and through flashbacks. I suppose one of comparisons between <i>The Dinner</i> and the Gillian Flynn-novel-that-will-not-be-named emerges from the fact I couldn't write a review of either without fearing revealing spoilers. Koch's novel is tighter, however, in its focus on familiar relationships, whether they be father/son, mother/son, father/mother, or brother/brother. The narrators gets to articulate the terrific hatred and frustration inherent in minor interactions and (perhaps) over-sensitivity to slights and manipulation when one's mind isn't quite in the right place. And the deep darkness connects to the question of whether or not families can retain a semblance of normalcy or even grow closer when the stakeholders lie, scheme, and withhold, sometimes to each other, sometimes for each other.<br /><br />I very much enjoyed <i>The Dinner</i>. I don't re-read much but I could see myself re-reading the novel in a month or two because the elegant structure deserves a second look. This book is better than its the "European <i>Gone Girl</i> or "topic of countless dinner party debates" horseshit tag lines. Read <i>The Dinner</i> on its own terms.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2052585462198221569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1070357496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070357496" />
    <a title="Debbie &quot;DJ&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12620745-debbie-dj"><img alt="Debbie &quot;DJ&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407426768p2/12620745.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070357496?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie &quot;DJ&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie &quot;DJ&quot;" href="/user/show/12620745-debbie-dj">Debbie &quot;DJ&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12620745-debbie-dj?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12620745-debbie-dj?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12620745-debbie-dj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070357496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13950092951526765747">This is the book that should have said, "If you liked Gone Girl..." And, after reading some reviews, maybe it did, and I just never saw it. For me, this book is a top notch psychological thriller.<br/><br/>Two couples meet at a posh restaurant for dinner, arriving to discuss some type of problem with their children. The two couples are Paul, and his wife Clair, and Serge (Paul's brother), and his wife Babette. Paul is the single narrator of this story and he recounts much of his past as each course of din</span>
  <span id="freeText13950092951526765747" style="display:none">This is the book that should have said, "If you liked Gone Girl..." And, after reading some reviews, maybe it did, and I just never saw it. For me, this book is a top notch psychological thriller.<br /><br />Two couples meet at a posh restaurant for dinner, arriving to discuss some type of problem with their children. The two couples are Paul, and his wife Clair, and Serge (Paul's brother), and his wife Babette. Paul is the single narrator of this story and he recounts much of his past as each course of dinner arrives. I don't think I'll ever get their waiters pointy little finger out of my head, as he uses it to point to each item of food as it arrives. You know, those fancy restaurants who call three slices of cheese on a plate the most extraordinary cuisine, with each described meticulously. <br /><br />Sorry, the story...The first 20% or so focuses on Paul's memories and how he, and each of the characters have interacted in the past. It seems to plod along a bit, however, later, the fleshing out of these characters proves vital.<br /><br />Here's what happened after the first 20%, BAM!! WHAT? WHAT JUST HAPPENED? The "problem" related to their children, begins to be reveled, and I was in complete shock. From this point on, I was riveted to my chair, reading at record speed, with a lot of OMG's! What the children were involved in, and the parent's ideals and backgrounds really come into play now with how the situation will be handled. <br /><br />What I liked so much is the extremely uncomfortable questions the author wants us to ponder, such as: Do our moral responsibilities lie with the protection of our family, or with the larger picture of societies morals? Can violence be hereditary? Do we all have a private and a public face? Are "real" families only those with similar genes? Is a happy family one that sticks together at all costs? Are certain people valued more because of their social standing or intelligence? Do we have a secret vigilante wish to kill those who cannot be rehabilitated, and where do we draw that line?<br /><br />I love that this book took me down the dark side. I didn't like a single character, but sure did love the book. So, if you'd like your Gone Girl a little darker, you won't be disappointed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13950092951526765747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2004332705" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004332705" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004332705?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20510036-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004332705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9844537198801513203">The folks in this book got under my skin from the get go. The pretentiousness was mind boggling. These are people for whom it's important who arrives last for a dinner reservation, for whom appearance is all. They meet at a restaurant that reminds me of The Emperor's New Clothes. Will no one admit to the laughingly almost empty plates of unique ingredients? And it goes downhill from there. These aren't people you're going to like. Those opening chapters give you an inkling of how these folks wil</span>
  <span id="freeText9844537198801513203" style="display:none">The folks in this book got under my skin from the get go. The pretentiousness was mind boggling. These are people for whom it's important who arrives last for a dinner reservation, for whom appearance is all. They meet at a restaurant that reminds me of The Emperor's New Clothes. Will no one admit to the laughingly almost empty plates of unique ingredients? And it goes downhill from there. These aren't people you're going to like. Those opening chapters give you an inkling of how these folks will deal with the horrendous thing their boys have done. <br /><br />We see everything through the eyes of Paul, but that doesn't mean you like him. <br />I can't see this book being made into a movie. So much of the “dialog” is Paul talking directly to the reader, giving you his opinion on events. And as the book goes on, you start questioning the man's sanity. <br /><br />I am reading this for book club and am anxious for the discussion. This is definitely one of those books where you don't care for the characters but there's lots of meat to discuss. It's not an easy read, definitely not a feel good. But it does grip you and force you to think how you would act in a similar situation. Hopefully not like these four parents…<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9844537198801513203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1424224172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424224172" />
    <a title="Glenn Sumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28854579-glenn-sumi"><img alt="Glenn Sumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444333567p2/28854579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424224172?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Sumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Sumi" href="/user/show/28854579-glenn-sumi">Glenn Sumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28854579-glenn-sumi?shelf=not-usa-can-uk">not-usa-can-uk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424224172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7755035993378991458">There’s a bit too much on the menu in this wickedly fun psychological thriller from bestselling Dutch author Herman Koch.<br/><br/>But he’s such a good writer (which comes through in the smooth translation), and his narrator is so savagely funny, insightful and demented that the entire thing goes down like an excellent meal – with a slightly nasty aftertaste because of the subject matter.<br/><br/>Two middle-aged couples dine out at an expensive Amsterdam restaurant. As they go through each extravagant, rather absu</span>
  <span id="freeText7755035993378991458" style="display:none">There’s a bit too much on the menu in this wickedly fun psychological thriller from bestselling Dutch author Herman Koch.<br /><br />But he’s such a good writer (which comes through in the smooth translation), and his narrator is so savagely funny, insightful and demented that the entire thing goes down like an excellent meal – with a slightly nasty aftertaste because of the subject matter.<br /><br />Two middle-aged couples dine out at an expensive Amsterdam restaurant. As they go through each extravagant, rather absurd course (presided over by a memorable restaurant worker who points at things with his pinky!), we flash back to scenes involving their children. The quartet are dining out to discuss an incident that may affect everyone’s future.<br /><br />Despite the contrived setting – I doubt they would meet in such a public way to talk about such a sensitive, private matter – the book is cleverly constructed. And narrator Paul, a former history teacher who resents his boorish older brother Serge’s political success, plays with our sympathies. <br /><br />At first we’re on Paul’s side; he’s amusing, self-deprecating and his cutting social observations (about the restaurant, about his brother) seem as sharp as a chef's knife. But as the night goes on and he fills us in on his past – and that of his wife, Claire, and his son, Michel – things become more sinister. Then they become downright creepy. <br /><br />The disturbing act at the centre of the book brings up lots of ethical and moral questions, and Koch handles the teasing out of this incident brilliantly. He’s less successful near the end, where he practically rushes through to the denouement. <br /><br />But the jagged little pieces of this narrative fit together into one horrific portrait of family life. I’m definitely going to read Koch’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18594633.Summer_House_with_Swimming_Pool" title="Summer House with Swimming Pool by Herman Koch" rel="nofollow noopener"> Summer House With Swimming Pool</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7755035993378991458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_534030105" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/534030105" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/534030105?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=modern-fiction">modern-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer534030105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4003791552851912455">Wow, lots to unpack here. <br/><br/>This is a novel that has been sitting on my shelf for several years, and I finally pulled it down in a good-faith effort to read more of the books I already own. I don't remember why I was so interested in this that I bought a copy, so I skimmed some reviews to jog my memory. I saw everything from 1 star to 5 stars from Goodreads friends, with some very heated comments about the characters and the story. It lowered my expectations, and I felt ready to tackle this book.<br/><br/>B</span>
  <span id="freeText4003791552851912455" style="display:none">Wow, lots to unpack here. <br /><br />This is a novel that has been sitting on my shelf for several years, and I finally pulled it down in a good-faith effort to read more of the books I already own. I don't remember why I was so interested in this that I bought a copy, so I skimmed some reviews to jog my memory. I saw everything from 1 star to 5 stars from Goodreads friends, with some very heated comments about the characters and the story. It lowered my expectations, and I felt ready to tackle this book.<br /><br />But something funny happened on the way to this review... I didn't hate the book. Instead, I got engrossed in the novel and wanted to see how it ended. The story is that two couples are meeting at an expensive restaurant for dinner. One of the couples is our narrator and his wife, Claire; the other is Serge, a politician (and the brother of our narrator), and Serge's wife, Babette. Both couples have teenage sons, and the dinner meeting is to discuss something horrible the children did. Our narrator doesn't like his brother and often tries to antagonize him, which adds more tension to the conversation.<br /><br />The novel is organized by the courses of a dinner: Apertif, Appetizer, Main Course, etc. The events take place over the course of one evening, with a few flashbacks to important events. I wasn't surprised to learn that the author has a background in acting, because while reading this novel I could envision it as a dramatic play. (Or a movie, which is apparently being released soon. It was dumb luck that I read this book so close to the film's debut.) <br /><br />All we know is what our narrator tells us, and at times he and his memories are unreliable. Many reviewers have commented on how unlikable all of the characters are, which is true -- they are selfish, vain, and inconsiderate, and our narrator's family is especially violent and has anger management issues -- but really, our society seems fascinated by such sociopaths. They are the subject of countless movies and bestselling books, and we love to hate them (or elect them president, but that's another story).<br /><br />In this book, we're inside a sociopath's head. Our narrator is sharing how he views the world, and it is fascinating. Of course we don't condone his actions, but he seems rather calm and rational, up until the moment he starts beating you.<br /><br />While I ended up getting involved in the story, this was a difficult novel to read because of the violence and brutal descriptions. I frequently winced while reading, or had to pause to take a breath. Our narrator makes some amusing comments, but even his humor becomes snarky and bitter.<br /><br />As disturbing as it was, I did appreciate this novel and its theme of exploring how far parents will go to protect a child, but I'm not sure I would widely recommend this book. It's definitely not for the faint of heart, and you'll be disappointed if you expect any of the characters to grow and become better people. This is a dark family story -- it's all villains and no heroes.<br /><br /><b>Amusing Passage:</b><br /> <blockquote> <br />When the conversation turns too quickly to films, I see it as a sign of weakness. I mean: films are more something for the end of the evening, when you really don't have much else to talk about. I don't know why, but when people start talking about films, I always get a sinking feeling in the pit of my stomach, like when you wake up in the morning and find that it's already getting dark outside.<br /><br />The worst are those people who describe entire films. They get right into it -- they have no qualms about taking up fifteen minutes of your time; fifteen minutes per film, that is. They don't really care whether you haven't seen the film in question or whether you saw it a long time ago. Such considerations don't bother them -- they're already right in the middle of the opening scene. To be polite, you feign interest at first, but soon you bid farewell to courtesy: You yawn openly, stare at the ceiling, and squirm around in your chair. You do everything in your power to make the narrator shut up, but nothing helps. They're too far gone to notice the signals. Above all, they're addicted to themselves and their own crap about films.<br /></blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4003791552851912455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_585020236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585020236" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585020236?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=psychological-thrillers">psychological-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585020236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8870155201560073588">The Dinner by Herman is certainly a quirky and entertaining read and if you like dark, quirky and different then this one may be for you. I really enjoyed this novel, it certainly packs a punch.<br/><br/>Take two families, a dinner setting and a couple dangerously delinquent sons and a very disturbing act of criminality that has shocked the nation and you have yourself the plot of a very well written novel.<br/><br/>A word of warning! Not every reader is going to love this one...............so if you dislike storie</span>
  <span id="freeText8870155201560073588" style="display:none">The Dinner by Herman is certainly a quirky and entertaining read and if you like dark, quirky and different then this one may be for you. I really enjoyed this novel, it certainly packs a punch.<br /><br />Take two families, a dinner setting and a couple dangerously delinquent sons and a very disturbing act of criminality that has shocked the nation and you have yourself the plot of a very well written novel.<br /><br />A word of warning! Not every reader is going to love this one...............so if you dislike stories with dislikeable characters and unreliable narrators and dark happenings, stay clear. On the other hand if you like dark novels like Gone Girl and Defending Jacob and we need to talk about Kevin I think you will enjoy this book.<br /><br />There are some great lines in this book;<br /><br /><i> You say something so razor-sharp that the person you say it to carries it around with them for the rest of their life.<br /><br />When the conversation turns too quickly to films, I see it as a sign of weakness, I mean films are more something for the end of the evening, when you dont have much else to talk about.</i><br /><br />I loved the premise of this novel, how far parents will go to protect a child and it really is a book that gets you thinking, What IF...<br />This is a book that asks difficult questions and the plot is slow but shocking, I especially loved the build-up to the revelations and the way in which the story was narrated by Paul. This Novel would make an excellent book club read, as the characters and revelations make for excellent discussion. I could imagine a book club getting great mileage out of this one.<br /><br />A great read and a very thought provoking novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8870155201560073588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_544948600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544948600" />
    <a title="Pattie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3013441-pattie"><img alt="Pattie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581962924p2/3013441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544948600?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pattie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pattie" href="/user/show/3013441-pattie">Pattie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780770437855" href="/book/show/15797938-the-dinner">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544948600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5292655767332803752">I couldn't wait for this book to be publshed in the U.S. but I wound up being very disappointed in it. To begin with, the character who narrates the book comes across as petty, childish, and irritating from the opening pages. He was never a sympathetic character, although I believe he initially was supposed to be, in comparison to his brother. The brother, a boorish, pompous and larger than life figure, actually had more heart in the long run. In addition, I didn't find it believable that these </span>
  <span id="freeText5292655767332803752" style="display:none">I couldn't wait for this book to be publshed in the U.S. but I wound up being very disappointed in it. To begin with, the character who narrates the book comes across as petty, childish, and irritating from the opening pages. He was never a sympathetic character, although I believe he initially was supposed to be, in comparison to his brother. The brother, a boorish, pompous and larger than life figure, actually had more heart in the long run. In addition, I didn't find it believable that these two couples, related by blood, would go to a high end restaurant where one member of the foursome is a well-known up and coming politician to discuss a private, disturbing, life-altering matter regarding their children. Wouldn't they simply meet at one of their houses to discuss this? Some of the events that unfold and personality traits that are revealed are somewhat over the top. One of the four would already either be institutionalized or behind bars for prior actions described. The buildup is not as expected or should be. I felt cheated by this book and the fact that all the characters lack such a moral compass. The ones who show a flash of morality near the end have it quickly snuffed out by the other characters. It is a decidedly unsatisfying, and not very believable, read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5292655767332803752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wt+JHkhBAstIgKAnJHUb3lB+JdVKNVPF+nQjmXg5ymEtBdy2P2jcrUO4xMPd94LMt2E7SQ0llKS0f3bZBJo7BQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kxNB70zTFtdGHKiZzpr5Ar99inEGSqsnPadK1EX57BjkyRRHO/rIsU0kzH03GGAQWGKU7UFabEZzrB+UOVodfA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10285992954161413846">Herman Koch (1953) is known as a television producer and a writer. The book 'Het diner', published in 2009, was his breakthrough in the Netherlands. It was published in 17 countries. It was partly based on a true story involving a homeless woman named, María del Rosario Endrinal Petit, in Barcelona (Spain), in December 2005. <br/><br/>Koch was born in Arnhem, and later moved to Amsterdam. He studied Russian</span>
  <span id="freeText10285992954161413846" style="display:none">Herman Koch (1953) is known as a television producer and a writer. The book 'Het diner', published in 2009, was his breakthrough in the Netherlands. It was published in 17 countries. It was partly based on a true story involving a homeless woman named, María del Rosario Endrinal Petit, in Barcelona (Spain), in December 2005. <br /><br />Koch was born in Arnhem, and later moved to Amsterdam. He studied Russian for some months, and lived in Finland for a while. Nowadays he is married to the Spanish Amalia, and has a son, Pablo (1994).<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10285992954161413846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
